Food

Futures in Flour and Wheat Fall Uniformly

After the flour market opened in the morning, the market showed a uniform downward trend in all months. Quotes for foreign wheat fell by approximately 0.10-0.20 yuan in Chicago and approximately 0.04 yuan in Canada. The market price was initially stable, but the actual sales in the north remained sluggish. The quoted price for spot flour in Tianjin was only 3.52 to 3.50 yuan. This new price caused a uniform loosening of sentiment inside and outside the industry. Bullish investors from Yingkou, Northeast China, sold off their positions, and funds were released into the market. Therefore, the opening prices for all months fell significantly. When the afternoon market opened, due to the stagnation of actual sales and very little buying interest, the sentiment among industry participants was largely weak. As a result, the market situation for all months continued to fall. The Mid-Autumn Festival season is coming to an end, and the purchasing power in various places is naturally declining. Therefore, the market feels very easy to loosen. As a result, the current month fell by 0.035 yuan compared to the previous week, October fell by 0.0525 yuan, November fell by 0.05 yuan, December fell by 0.0525 yuan, January fell by 0.04 yuan, and February fell by 0.045 yuan.

After the wheat market opened in the morning, the market situation in all months generally showed a flat and soft trend. Quotes for foreign wheat fell by approximately 0.10-0.20 yuan in Chicago and approximately 0.04 yuan in Canada. Market sentiment was already weak at the opening because factories showed no interest in purchasing the standard wheat, and spot goods in the market were so abundant. It was not easy to boost outside industry sentiment. Furthermore, after rainfall in various places, the food panic eased somewhat. In terms of rice prices, they also fell significantly from their peak. Therefore, market sentiment gradually weakened, and the market felt looser step by step. When the afternoon market opened, because the flour market had declined, market sentiment was even more sluggish, and buyers were even scarcer. As a result, the decline in all months was also quite large. As a result, September and October fell by 0.09 yuan compared to the previous week, November fell by 0.08 yuan, December fell by 0.13 yuan, January fell by 0.08 yuan, and February fell by 0.10 yuan. The spot wheat market has not been active because flour sales have been flat, and factories have been very unwilling to purchase.

Yesterday, 3

Reduction of Railway Freight Rates and Development of Rural Economy (7) by Wu Shaozeng 8

For joint transportation goods, the freight revenue each railway should receive can be proportionally distributed based on the mileage the goods traveled on each line.

The above suggestion breaks various restrictions such as distance (referring to long distances exceeding 500 kilometers) and basic freight rates. Some may consider it shocking. In reality, this type of freight rate is similar to the "Blanket Rates" or "Postage Stamp Rates" that have been prevalent in the United States for a long time. In June 1898, American railways implemented blanket rates (i.e., charging the same freight rate regardless of the route taken), applicable to both classified and unclassified goods. For example, for goods transported from the Missouri River to the Atlantic coast, the freight rate is determined by the blanket rate system, regardless of whether the origin is near the Missouri River or the Atlantic coast. Similarly, goods transported westward within New England are also calculated based on blanket rates, with the intention of enabling New England manufacturers to transport goods westward and compete favorably with factories near raw material production areas, preventing the decline of New England's prosperity. The goods to which blanket rates apply include those easily absorbed by water transportation. For instance, leather shoes produced in Boston in the east, if transported to San Francisco in the west, can follow two routes: one via the transcontinental railway and the other via waterway through the Panama Canal to San Francisco. To prevent the railway from losing this transportation business to waterways, it implements blanket rates. Furthermore, if oranges from California in the west are transported to New York for sale, they will inevitably compete with oranges from Florida in the southeast. If charged at regular freight rates, California orange merchants would be deterred due to losses, and railway transportation and people's consumption would also be affected. Therefore, blanket rates are also applied to such goods. (To be continued)

Reading Q&A

Explanation of Contradiction (Continued) 9

Answers to Wu Zuocheng and Feng Qiaojun

"Xié háng" (頡頏) means "incompatible." For example, in a war, either you lose or I lose; there is no way for both sides to win. This is "xié háng." The two sides of "xié háng" are completely impossible to unify. Therefore, "xié háng" is merely the opposite, not a contradiction. The two sides of a contradiction, at a certain time, can be compatible, even mutually dependent. This has been pointed out in the previous examples of private life and ideals. However, we cannot say that contradictions are always compatible; they are only compatible at certain times. For example, the chick inside the egg and the eggshell are contradictory. The chick must break the eggshell to come out. This is the resolution of the contradiction. However, before the chick grows to be able to act independently, it can be accommodated within the eggshell and even requires the protection of the eggshell. Therefore, the contradiction between the chick and the eggshell is only compatible before the chick grows up. Once the chick has grown up, it becomes incompatible. Therefore, contradiction and incompatibility are not completely different things. Contradictions only become absolutely incompatible when they develop or grow to their extreme. Before this point, they are still compatible. The meaning of "xié háng," however, is absolute incompatibility. People who see contradiction as "xié háng" believe that whenever they encounter opposing things, they must immediately fight to the death, refusing to calmly adapt to the development trends of things and take appropriate actions. For example, when the chick has not yet grown, it should have been hatched by the hen, but instead, they are eager to break the eggshell. This behavior not only fails to resolve the contradiction but also kills the potential chick. Using the example of life and ideals, if someone believes that life and ideals are contradictory, they immediately abandon ideals and only care about short-term gains, not knowing that there is a possibility of achieving ideals through the practice of life. This is the drawback of mistaking contradiction for "xié háng."

Contradiction is a constantly developing opposing action within unity. The resolution of contradiction is only achieved when it develops to a certain degree.

Little Western Paradise 11

— by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 1: A Ghost Carries a Cart from Guanzhong, a Lonely Traveler Crosses the Rapids, and a Ferryman Mourns the People of Qin

However, there was one thing that Li Shilian found particularly interesting: between the houses with dismantled roofs, there were still houses with yellow earthen walls and wooden doors. On the wooden door hung a plaque, the very plaque of the Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Collection Sub-Office of a certain district of a certain county of a certain province. He couldn't help but exclaim "Oh." He thought to himself that the tobacco and alcohol tax still had great potential. But his "Oh" had already alarmed everyone in the car. Cheng Zhiqian said, "Mr. Li, what are your thoughts?" Li Shilian said, "I feel that even in relatively lively places, there are still such houses. Who knows what it's like elsewhere?" Secretary Chang said, "Don't look at how desolate this place is. It is said to be near the capital of the Qin Kingdom. Thousands of years ago, Emperor Qin unified China here and built the Great Wall. To say that the present is not as good as the past, it's really not turning the clock back." Cheng Zhiqian said, "The Qin capital, Xianyang? Have we arrived at Xianyang yet?" Secretary Chang said, "Look, isn't that the ancient ferry of Xianyang?" As he spoke, the car rolled over a small slope and onto the inner mudflat. Sure enough, there was a river in front of them, the water a muddy yellow. On the southwest corner of the river, there was a semi-circle of yellow earth slope. On the side facing the river, two slender arrow towers jutted out from the earthen wall, one tall and one short, one far and one near, complementing each other. The car drove straight to the riverbank, and the current seemed very swift. Four or five ferries were moored on the riverbank, looking very strange. They had no awnings but were flat, and vehicles and mules could cross on them. The bow and stern were both square. If the stern wasn't slightly higher, it would look just like an enlarged square-toed shoe. A larger ferry came over from the other side and docked at the shore. Two sedans were parked on the deck, as well as four or five carrying poles. Among them was a girl of sixteen or seventeen, wearing a straight-striped blue cloth short jacket, with two silver earrings hanging from her ears. She was clearly a country girl, but she had cut her hair short. When she saw this car, which was a sedan type, different from the cargo and passenger cars running on the main road, she just stared. When she happened to see Cheng Zhiqian also sizing her up, she lowered her head and walked away. (16)

Tomb of Zhuge Jin 13

— Chen Jingyu

In the southwest corner of Xianxi, Fengxian, no more than two li away, there is an ancient tomb. The villagers call it the Zhuge Tomb.

What is the construction of this tomb like? Due to the passage of time, it is deeply sunk into the ground and cannot be seen. Only a mound of wasteland and a stone stele of the tomb ridge remain.

The tablet system is very simple, only engraving the five characters "Tomb of Zhuge Jin" in the size of a bowl mouth, the font is definitely not Han Li, but a very clumsy form of true script, so at first glance, it is almost suspected to come from the good people's transmission. According to the legends of the elders in the countryside, regarding the history of this tomb, there is a story similar to mythology:

During the "Tianqi" period of the late Ming Dynasty, villagers cultivated here, and the ground suddenly collapsed, forming a cave. Entering it, it was very vast and dark, making it impossible to distinguish the path. Touching forward, the hand touched an object, which was cool to the bone. It was a stone wall! Advancing along the wall, reaching the end, he saw a jar of burning torches, the light blazing! Vaguely there was a room, like a hall, a huge coffin hanging in it, and in front of the coffin there was a table on which various unknown animal-shaped objects were listed. The villagers saw the situation and thought it was a ghost; therefore, they broke the jar with the farming tools they held, turned around and thought of escaping, their feet stumbled on a stone, fell to the ground, got up suddenly, broke it again, and ran away wildly. The story was spread to the countryside, and the viewers gathered! The village chief was afraid of causing trouble, and urgently reported to the county; the county magistrate came to examine it, and recited the inscription he destroyed, recognizing it as the burial place of Zhuge Ziyu in the Three Kingdoms: Therefore, he ordered the servants to block the hole, and set up a stone to record it, that is, the one that stands on the tomb today!

According to the ancients, when the coffin was being buried, a huge jar was often used in front of the coffin, half-filled with lacquer oil, and lit with cotton rope, closed in the soil, even if the air was isolated, it would never be extinguished, and the lacquer oil would not dry up; its name was called "Everlasting Light!" Extremely ancient tombs are almost nineteen out of ten; it is only because the villagers are ignorant, have little knowledge and are strange, so that the ancient objects before thousands of years have suddenly suffered the misfortune of destruction! How unfortunate is it not?

Child Training 14

— Xie

The five-year-old girl in the pavilion room went to the alley with the eleven-year-old boy in the front building in the evening to play. There were many people cooling off in the alley, squeezing out and stopping, and the girl was knocked down, her little buttocks just sitting in the sewage, so that the clothes that had just been bathed and changed were stained with mud. The eleven-year-old boy hurried to help her back. When the girl's mother saw that her child's clothes were dirty, she couldn't help but get angry and slapped her in the face, causing the girl to cry loudly. At the same time, she scolded: Why are you going to play with bad kids? The sister-in-law in the front building heard that her son had caused trouble to other people's children, and scolded her son for being a bad kid, so she got so angry that she couldn't breathe, pulled her son to the sister-in-law's pavilion room, and punished him to kneel down and apologize. The child didn't listen, so she grabbed his ear and took him back to the front building, and then closed the door. People downstairs only heard the sound of "patting" upstairs, and the sound of the child crying, and the sound of the sister-in-law scolding, echoed together. This sound continued for a long time, and the people downstairs hurried up to persuade them, but the sister-in-law had already closed the door very tightly and could not be knocked open wildly. Moreover, the sound of "patting" inside became tighter and louder, the child's cry became louder and more miserable, and the sister-in-law's scolding became more and more urgent and higher. Someone on the opposite balcony looked down at the sister-in-law's room, and only saw the sister-in-law with disheveled hair, holding a two-foot-long rattan whip, and slashing up and down at the child with murderous intent. The child staggered up and down, blocking with both hands up and down, and his tragic cries sounded like a pig being slaughtered with a knife. The people on the balcony really couldn't bear to see it, and shouted to stop. The sister-in-law heard the persuasion, as if adding fuel to the fire, and the murderous appearance became even more terrible, and the whip was more densely covered like raindrops. The child rolled on the floor, and the people on the balcony hurriedly retreated to avoid increasing the sister-in-law's anger and causing the child to suffer more, but the sound of "patting" still did not stop, and the cries of anger and scolding also played together. After about six or seven minutes, the sound of "patting" gradually thinned out and disappeared, and the cries of anger and scolding also gradually subsided into the darkness.

The next day, the child was still able to come downstairs to walk around, but the bare upper body was covered with purplish-black scars, countless hundreds of them, and there were also countless purplish-black strips under both knees. The part above the knees was invisible because the pants covered them. Alas, the child training of Chinese mothers!

— Yin Juan

Penglai Pavilion 16

— Yu Hong

In the past, perhaps not many people paid attention to Penglai Pavilion. It was only because General Feng Yuxiang, the Christian general, made a special trip to visit it this spring, which made this scenic spot, which was buried in Donglu, gradually become popular.

Penglai Pavilion is located about one li outside the north gate of Penglai County, Jiaodong. (The opening of The Travels of Lao Ts'an says that Penglai Pavilion is outside the east gate of Penglai County. This old man must have turned around.) It is located on a mountain and faces the water, and the terrain is extremely beautiful. The so-called "Dan Cliff Wonderland" refers to this. In addition to Penglai Pavilion, there are many other temples on this mountain, and there are also many inscriptions by famous people of past dynasties. Su Xueshi Dongpo once served as a prime minister here, so he also added a lot of beautiful stories to the lake and mountains. Now, the statue of this old gentleman is still sitting upright in the temple, receiving the respect of tourists.

To the west of the pavilion is Chengbixuan, and to the east is Guanlanting. Both are places for tourists to rest and a good place to escape the heat. Whenever the sun sets, overlooking from the window, Changshan is in sight, and fishermen's songs fill the ears. There is a real feeling of wanting to become an immortal, so people often set up banquets here to meet friends during the hot summer.

In addition to Penglai Pavilion, Penglai County also has the other ten beautiful sceneries, such as "Bronze Well and Golden Waves," "Leaking Sky and Silver Rain," "Lion Cave and Smoke Clouds," "Ten Thousand Hectoliters of Pearls," "Mirage," "Sunrise Fusang," "Evening Tide and New Moon," "Fisherman's Dyke and Singing Table," "High Pavilion Lingkong," and "Ten Thousand Miles of Qingpo." However, some of them are famous but have no substance, but the "Mirage" is a rare beautiful scene.

Penglai Pavilion has long been in disrepair due to its age and is already dilapidated. When General Wu Fuwei was stationed in Zhongzhou, he once launched a renovation, but unfortunately, this plan could not be fully realized. Now, it has become the palace of the Eighth Grandpa soldiers, and tourists have no way to visit it.

White Ox Village 17

— Gao Jinyue

A snow-white ox, as white as snow, ambled across the fragrant grass embankment, appearing all the more solemn and tranquil.

Not far from the northern fence of Fengjing, a stream meandered, and trees cast shadows, creating a very serene and beautiful landscape. There was a small village called White Ox Village. It is said that during the Song Dynasty, the famous Chen Shunyu (a contemporary of Su Dongpo), tired of officialdom, built a few thatched huts here, tilling the land and studying. He often rode a white ox, and in the fields and on the embankments, he would happily recite poetry and play the flute, completely at ease. Later, Hong Kunxuan wrote a "Song of the White Ox Hermit Riding a Calf," describing his reclusive life:

A village of sedge grass, a boundless sight,

Ten miles of Jiangnan, spring intricately woven.

By the green maple path, as the sun sets,

He mounts a black ox, unrecognized.

Rice paddies and desolate lands, veiled in misty haze,

A light raincoat and short bamboo hat, enjoying the cool breeze.

East suburban rain clears, muddy path slick,

Four hooves crush the red flowers of the stream.

Having presented myriad words, he returns early,

The new laws of Xining are too hasty.

His distant teachings are reminiscent of He Fen,

Hemp and mulberry thrive by the good stream.

South Mountain white rocks, clear and cold water,

Who sings endlessly through the long night?

At dusk, halfway through the meal, under the bronze axle,

Tomorrow, he'll study scriptures, horns in sight.

After Shunyu's death, Su Dongpo wrote an article mourning him, showing the same deep affection as Ouyang Xiu's preface to Mei Shengyu's poetry collection.

As for the origin of White Ox Village, according to the village elders, "In the past, on moonlit nights, a large, ownerless white ox would appear here, squatting and chewing grass. Curious villagers would try to catch it, but it would quickly run into the pond and disappear. One time, a villager managed to grab its chain by the pond and desperately dragged it ashore, but the ox bit his leg. The villager only managed to retrieve a small piece of the chain, which turned out to be made of pure gold. He was overjoyed, but unfortunately, the wound never healed, and it wasn't until the piece of gold chain completely vanished that he died. Superstitious villagers reverently worshipped the white ox, calling the village White Ox Village and the pond White Ox Pond."

Of course, this mythical tale is not as verifiable as the documented accounts mentioned earlier.

The Scent of Imperial Incense, Faintly Lingering 18

— Original by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, Translated by Qin Shouou

At that moment, our chauffeur was focusing all his energy on his task, as he had been ordered by Qing Shan to ensure that the Empress Dowager's carriage stopped exactly in the center of the platform so that she could step onto the apricot-yellow felt mat when she alighted.

On this day, important officials from Tianjin and the surrounding areas, both civil and military, had arrived very early to await the imperial arrival. Each person, according to their rank, had dressed with as much care as possible. As a result, when we arrived, they were already lined up in a very long row. The red and green colors were dazzling, almost making it impossible to open one's eyes. As soon as they saw the imperial arrival, they knelt silently along the outer edge of the platform. Yuan Shikai himself was kneeling alone, prostrate in front of everyone else!

The train rolled slowly past them and finally came to a complete stop. I usually loved to watch a lively scene, but seeing these statue-like officials, I couldn't help but feel uncomfortable. Especially their expressions; one could say that not a single one was not unpleasant. Their heads were lowered past their chests, their eyes fixed on the ground, and they didn't even seem to dare to breathe, making it hard to believe that this was a genuine display of respect. However, their attire was still a beautiful spectacle. Most of them had peacock feather plumes on their hats. Peacock feathers were originally very beautiful, possessing their own radiance. Coupled with the strong sunlight that shone through the awning, all the peacock feathers seemed to turn into golden leaves, with brilliant golden light shimmering everywhere. Free Talk

Please Consider the Objective Environment 19

— Xu Maoyong

In Sichuan, there were two monks, one rich and one so poor that he only had a bowl and a begging cup. Once, they met and both said they wanted to make a pilgrimage to the South Sea. But the rich monk planned and planned, considering how much travel money to bring, what kind of ship to take, how to prepare his luggage, and whether there would be any dangers on the road. After much planning, he still couldn't make up his mind. After a year or two, he still couldn't set out. Who knew that during his indecision, the poor monk had already walked to the South Sea and returned.

The lesson of this story is that the power of subjective will can overcome the objective material environment. Peng Duanshu of the Qing Dynasty used this story to prove the following theory: "Are things in the world difficult or easy? If you do them, then the difficult becomes easy; if you don't do them, then the easy becomes difficult."

Indeed, this makes some sense. But what if the rich monk's will was as strong as the poor monk's? Undoubtedly, the South Sea would have let the rich monk arrive first, because he had money and traveling would be much easier for him.

Regarding the difficulty or ease of achieving something, the decisive power of the material environment is ultimately greater than everything else.

Opponents of the current Mass Language movement often say this: People who advocated vernacular Chinese during the May Fourth Movement were able to immediately produce vernacular writing, but those who advocate Mass Language now only know how to shout slogans and can't produce anything of substance. This shows the emptiness and boredom of the Mass Language movement—they think this is a powerful argument, but in fact, it's completely unreasonable.

We must understand that Mass Language is connected to all the problems of the masses. It is by no means simply a language reform movement; it is a movement within the larger movement to improve the entire life of the masses.

However, we must also know that the Mass Language movement and the Vernacular Chinese movement have two different aspects, which are their respective objective environments. During the May Fourth era, the bourgeois class was already quite powerful economically. Even the feudal warlords who monopolized political power at the time had to rely on them. At the same time, they used their own money to train their own intellectuals in universities at home and abroad. With economic power, their own cultural workers, and practical political movements, the success of the bourgeois class was naturally easier. Vernacular Chinese was created by the bourgeois class's own cultural workers, so it was naturally quick to produce.

Look at the masses connected to the current Mass Language movement. How can their economic lives and cultural levels be compared to those of the bourgeois class of that time? Isn't it too impatient to demand that they immediately produce Mass Language or Mass Culture? The rich monk in Sichuan can't afford a plane and certainly won't reach the South Sea in a few days.

The people who are now advocating Mass Language are not the cultural workers of the masses themselves. They only feel that Mass Language is something that should exist and can help the masses, so they are helping to create it. They are just helping and don't believe they can create a Mass Language model themselves. Authentic Mass Language can only be established by the masses themselves when their level is improved. Therefore, those who are demanding that the current advocates of Mass Language produce Mass Language are even more impatient.

The Mass Language movement is a difficult movement, but it is not something that cannot be successful. To succeed, we must first create a good objective environment.

From History to Collections 20

— Ling Mo

Although the compilation of Chinese historical books is not entirely satisfactory, the history section is already the most complete within the so-called four categories [of traditional Chinese bibliography]. The classics and philosophical works are hopeless, but fortunately, they won't be added to. The collection section is also a vast category, but it urgently needs reform.

The complete works of ancient Chinese people cannot be compared with the complete works of Western writers. Western writers mostly develop within a specialized field, while Chinese writers discuss everything. Take any of the complete works of Han, Liu, Ou, or Su, for example. There are official documents and social correspondence, but there must also be pure prose and poetry to show that the writer is a literati. Such complete works must be carefully selected and weeded out.

Writings such as imperial edicts, memorials, and petitions can mostly be found in books recording institutions of past dynasties, which have already been preserved. There is no need to preserve them in collections. Writings such as biographies and epitaphs only have value in historical terms. They should be compiled into books such as Collected Biographies and Epitaphs of Past Dynasties for use as historical materials. There is no need for them to have wide circulation. In addition, similar methods can be adopted for anything that does not belong to pure literature, leaving behind only a pure essence. Naturally, there are also some collection categories. Writings in the Taiping Guangji [an anthology of stories] were considered unimportant at the time, so they were rejected and set aside. Today, we should use the same method to set aside what we think should be set aside. This is a necessary general collection. As for general collections in the style of literary selections from past dynasties, they are optional.

Perhaps some people feel that complete works are also useful, but this won't cause any dispute. The existing editions of complete works should be enough to meet the needs of these people. We hope that the publishing industry will not always just reprint the same things.

Ah Yao Sees... 21

— TK

On Qi 22

— Kong Gong

Some years ago, someone said something like this: People in our scientific world only know about light gas and oxygen, but don't know about so-called "refined qi."

Those who only know about light gas, oxygen, and inert gas on one side, and those who only know about refined qi, vulgar qi, and clumsy qi on the other, are inevitably shocked by each other. These are mostly colorless and odorless, but the latter has no substance and cannot have an atomic weight, naturally burning or supporting combustion.

In times of conflict between the old and the new, the arguments on both sides tend to be extreme. Holding onto fifty miles, one cannot but attack a hundred miles, which is a matter of course. However, putting aside the merits of the battle, just looking at these words themselves, they are all somewhat pretentious.

Looking closely at those who burn test tubes and wield hammers, are they all just ordinary people who are ignorant of elegance and refinement, except for their mechanical lives? It is not so in the West; on the contrary, they have a better understanding of literature, an appreciation of art, and a comprehension of music. Their refinement and nobility are more widespread, greater, and more profound. On the one hand, science museums are built large; on the other hand, art galleries and music academies reach even higher.

Conversely, if this science of burning light gas and refining oxygen has no relation to life and no use, then this science is not worth studying. Science has its own truth, but it is not the only truth. All thoughts converge on one point, and all paths lead to the same destination. The future is aimed at human happiness. What is Buddhism without itself? What is science without life? There is really no need for any "debate" about such a simple truth.

If one lives in a house built by science, covers oneself with a blanket made by science, and eats medicine made by science when sick, can it be said that science does not dominate everything of mankind? It certainly dominates, but this did not fall from the moon or planets. It was created by mankind itself. It is mankind dominating everything of itself, and no one else or thing should be thanked. In addition to living in houses, covering oneself with blankets, and eating medicine, mankind also has other things to do.

Now it is understood that people in the scientific world are those who seek a state of happiness in life and who hope that mankind will reach a state of goodness and beauty. The debate over inert qi and refined qi, the debate over science and life, are all dry stakes.

True Essence of the Mass Language (Part 2) 23

— Li Jinxi

Furthermore, among the twenty Hinayana [Theravada] schools, the initial division into the "Mahāsāṃghika" [Great Community] and "Sthaviravāda" [Elders] schools, being mutually opposing, seemed to have a class nature, but in reality, it was due to different locations for the compilation of the scriptures (It is said that in the year of the Buddha's death, the scriptures were compiled in two places, inside and outside the cave. Inside the cave, there were many elders of the Sthaviravāda school, with Kāśyapa at the head, hence the name "Sthaviravāda"; outside the cave, there were many young monks, with no separate leader, hence the name "Mahāsāṃghika"). From then on, it evolved into a divergence in doctrines (It is said that a hundred years after the Buddha's death, the Bhikkhu Mahadeva appeared, and many descendants of the compilation outside the cave attached to him, hence taking the old name "Mahāsāṃghika"; those inside the cave opposed Mahadeva's teachings, so they also inherited the old name "Sthaviravāda." Later, the two schools further divided into eighteen schools, totaling twenty Hinayana schools). In short, "Mahāsāṃghika" became a common term for Buddhists after the Middle Ages, and its meaning is very egalitarian. It only requires one condition: Buddhist believers, even demons, humans, ghosts, or animals such as horses, cattle, chickens, and dogs, can all join this "Mahāsāṃghika" (When "Mahāsāṃghika" is added to other nouns, such as "Mahāsāṃghika seal," it refers to a seal used by a temple in common. There are quite a few other examples, such as the "Mahāsāṃghika adornment" in the Pure Land scriptures and the "Mahāsāṃghika awe of power" for novice Bodhisattvas, but I won't list them all).

(3) In modern common usage, "Mahāsāṃghika" simply means "the masses." Not only are there no class, religious, or racial restrictions, but they don't even have to gather in one place. Scattered people can sometimes also be called "Mahāsāṃghika." This meaning is commonly used and doesn't require examples. (When added to other nouns, such as the extremely vicious cursing term in southern dialects, "Mahāsāṃghika cub," it also proves this meaning.)

(4) In modern times, it is also used to translate Western "imported goods." "Mahāsāṃghika" is equivalent to the English "The masses" (or translated as "the crowd"). This original term already has a class nature (hence it is also translated as "the common people" or "the lower class"), originating in 1886 (the twelfth year of the Guangxu reign in the Qing Dynasty) when British Prime Minister Gladstone used this term as a relative term to "The Classes" (or translated as "the upper class"), thus forming a new trend in usage (see page 207 of volume six of the Oxford New English Dictionary). Recently, it has been gradually used for the majority of the collective people (such as the so-called "laboring masses," "proletarian masses," "peasant masses," etc.: when added to other nouns, labor unions are called "mass organizations," general strikes are called "mass strikes," collective coercion is called "mass action," and group movements that only seek daily benefits without regard to ideology are called "mass movements," etc.), seemingly returning to the old Chinese meaning (but this collective of farmers and workers is voluntary, although there are also those who are "requisitioned"): or used for the basic unit of a party (such as labor unions being called "mass organizations" in a vanguard party) and ordinary members in relation to cadres (also used by labor organizations). But when we use "Mahāsāṃghika" as an adjective and add it to other nouns, it is often equivalent to the English "Popular" (or translated as "common people's" or "vernacular"), and "Mass Language" is one of them. Forgive my ignorance, I have only seen "Popular" in English and have not found "Mass-laugnage" (Mass-literature—"Mass Literature" does exist, but it is ambiguous, and will be discussed in another section). In fact, those of us who are engaged in the National Language Movement only care about practical research work and do not crave new colored nouns like "Mass Language" because we can create them at will by piling up Chinese characters. But the ancients said it well: "Some follow old names, and some create new names." Since everyone is launching "new names" and happily discussing them, it is also acceptable to go along. However, the definition of "new names" must be agreed upon first. Based on the above-mentioned etymologies, I always feel that no matter what kind of "Mahāsāṃghika" is added to "Language," it immediately becomes "universal and equal," turning into the meaning of "Popularization" (because the meaning of the character "Language" is the "Language" of "speech," not the "Language" of "slogan"). "Names follow their masters," and the correct interpretation of "Mahāsāṃghika" should be the (3) definition that the current native masses have already become accustomed to: "Mahāsāṃghika is simply the masses." Then the true essence of "Mass Language" can be known!

But the matter is ultimately not that simple. I respectfully summarize the various current interpretations of "Mass Language" into three definitions, add comments to each, and create a short essay, which has already been published: (1) Does Mass Language really have "class nature"? (2) Is Mass Language contradictory to "dialect"? (3) Does Mass Language need a "standard language"?

Synthesizing the above three different definitions, weeding out the chaff and extracting the essence, understanding their purpose, and analyzing their logic, I summarize them into a few words to await judgment:

"Mass Language" is a standard dialect that is constructive and does not have class nature, existing in parallel with other "mother tongue" dialects that differ from the standard; it evolves with the times, expands with transportation, is enriched by culture, and beautified by literature and art: all of this is natural. We build "Mass Language" from an educational point of view, which is to unify the conflicts and contradictions between the consciousness of the "masses" who are lagging behind and the "masses" who are advancing, so that this standard dialect becomes a "common language" that "the majority of people in a country and nation can simultaneously understand and speak to each other."

If the definition of "Mass Language" is indeed like this, then I finally don't know what its similarities and differences are with "National Language" or "Vernacular"!

Originally, they are "the same in substance but different in name"!

Originally, all debates are just manipulating a few different names!

Originally, all problems cannot be practically solved without practical work.

In the previous section of this article published yesterday, on line eight from the top, the character "Language" was omitted below "occupational use," and on line thirty-five, the character "place" was omitted between "city wall." Also, on line twenty-five from the top, "ancient already has three," the three is a mistake for "of"; on line thirty-six, "Zhang Fu" is a mistake for "Zhang Fu"; on line thirty-eight, "Scholar Gong" is a mistake for "Soil Gong"; on line six from the bottom, the word "hua" in "official instruction" is a mistake for "gu"; on line twenty-five, "four big already on," "big" is a mistake for "person," and is hereby corrected.

Melancholy 24

— Hu Jinxu

Gently, quietly, lift the melancholy curtain, just a small corner, enough for melancholy eyes to peek out. Melancholy banana trees rustle in the wind, without rain, they seem to take pleasure in evil. Do not shake down the worn-out, tattered leaves, do not disturb the cold shadows on the ground, do not awaken the aging nightingale, urging a mournful, intermittent dirge. Faint clouds, sparse clouds, surround the autumn moon. The autumn moon sighs, coldly glancing at the autumn courtyard. Its radiance has been lost, like the congealed tears of a widow, quietly lying in the discolored corners of her eyes, only blurred and faint, forming a piece of melancholy. A melancholy heart is saddened, and the melancholy curtain is lowered, gently, quietly.

The Puppet State Sacrifices to Confucius 25

— Yu Gong

Confucius is in luck this year. The grand ceremony of sacrificing to Confucius is rare since the Republic of China. Now, the puppet state also wants to hold a grand ceremony.

When I was a child, Confucius' birthday was just a day off from school. Society had nothing to do with it. The wild grass in the Confucian temples in the city not only grew in the courtyard, but also on the hall, and no one cared about it. Now it's different. They have been renovated and look brand new. On the day of the sacrifice to Confucius, grand ceremonies were held in Confucian temples in various provinces. People from military, political, party, academic, and business circles gathered to perform rituals and used ancient music and instruments to promote the classics. This is a phenomenon of national revival. The elderly and young people are all happy, and even Confucius will smile when he eats cold meat.

However, it is reported that the puppet organization has also decided to sacrifice to Confucius on September 13th, forcing the puppet provincial and municipal government offices to hold grand commemorations on that day. All officials above the section chief level of the puppet organs will participate, and the so-called Wangdao Education Film will be shown. When this news reaches the ears of the people of the Republic of China, we should pay attention to it.

What we should pay attention to is: Is the puppet organization worthy of holding a grand ceremony of sacrificing to Confucius, and also showing Wangdao's educational film?

Confucius wrote the "Spring and Autumn Annals, and the rebellious ministers and traitors were afraid." What are the so-called rebellious ministers and traitors? Puyi, Zheng Xiaoxu, and others are undoubtedly standard rebellious ministers and traitors. According to the theory of the New Text School of the Han Dynasty in the late Qing Dynasty, Confucius's learning was originally the doctrine of "following Zhou," so he said, "How luxuriant is its culture! I follow Zhou." Until he defended himself and opposed Lu, Confucius's learning greatly changed. He knew that the Zhou Dynasty's system was determined by a group of emperors, princes, and high officials, protecting themselves and oppressing the common people. Therefore, he changed it to the doctrine of "valuing the people" and wanted to make his own rituals and music. So he also said that he would follow the time of Xia, ride the chariot of Yin, and wear the crown of Zhou, reforming and changing the law, which is obvious. He also wrote the "Spring and Autumn Annals." It can be seen from the words that everyone has the right to participate in national politics and cannot allow a group of nobles to do whatever they want. He first set an example himself, praising those who should be praised and criticizing those who should be criticized, like an emperor awarding rewards and punishments. In fact, this duty of awarding rewards and punishments originally belonged to the people. They have been used to reversing it, and Confucius used the "Spring and Autumn Annals" to turn it over. --The New Text School of the Han Dynasty in the late Qing Dynasty based its theory on Gongyang Gao, who praised Confucius as a populist politician. In today's terms, Confucius was a revolutionary who sought the interests of the masses. (It is not certain that the words Confucius said in the "Analects" were still the mass language of that time.)

Perhaps the reason why our Republic of China respects and sacrifices to Confucius is because he was a revolutionary who sought the interests of the masses? Then, the puppet organization, that is, Manchukuo, now also respects and sacrifices to Confucius and is still promoting Wangdao. Isn't this a contradictory and ridiculous thing? The puppet organization's Manchukuo system is monarchical--Puyi's becoming an executive is not enough, he insists on being an emperor, which is clear evidence. Confucius's learning is truly beneficial to democratic countries. Only our Republic of China is qualified to respect and sacrifice to Confucius. That puppet organization Manchukuo is not qualified to respect and sacrifice to Confucius. Moreover, that puppet organization Manchukuo is a puppet of others, doing whatever it wants, "oppressing the common people," and has become a tool for the puppet show's string pullers, raising horses and training soldiers everywhere to provoke. How can it be worthy of any Wangdao?

However, the puppet organization Manchukuo also respects and sacrifices to Confucius. What is the intention? Originally, the first principle of Confucianism is to respect the emperor. Even according to the theory of modern Confucianism, although Confucius was a populist, he was a populist who absolutely obeyed under the emperor, just like the doctrine of Jesus, which requires civilians to pursue freedom and equality within the scope of obedience to the emperor. That is to say, civilians "have the right to participate in national politics," but only with the emperor's permission. Now, the puppet organization Manchukuo claims to be a monarchical system. They can just use this point of Confucius's learning to sell their policy of deceiving the people. Therefore, the puppet organization Manchukuo also wants to respect and sacrifice to our Chinese Confucius. As for Wangdao's education, it is the best tool for the puppet organization Manchukuo to anesthetize our compatriots in the Northeast. How can they not use it?

From this point of view, although Confucius smiles to us in China, he is very unhappy with the puppet state.

Record of the Skin Party 26

— Lao Chui

The establishment of our party has a long history, with its origins dating back to the Guangxu and Xuantong eras. I am a later member, so I do not have in-depth knowledge of the party's founding history.

The purpose of our party is completely different from the San Kai Party, the Communist Party, the Axe Gang, the "Chai Bai" Party (confidence tricksters) etc. Our party takes "skin talk" (frivolous banter) as its core principle, hence the name "Skin Party." The members of our party include Liao Afeng, Zhu Asan, Tao Niu, Zhu Dakuaitou, and myself, though I'm probably still just a minor role player. (The above names are mostly special nicknames for our party comrades.)

The party's platform follows the "Six No's" doctrine: no politics, no society, no officialdom, no economics, no proper serious talk, and no discussion of painful or tragic events. The qualifications for joining are also very simple: just an introduction from one or more members, and the ability to say three lines of "skin talk." If someone can be called a pig, a nobody, or an embarrassment without blushing or becoming flustered, they are qualified.

Due to a lack of funds, our party has no fixed meeting place. Therefore, gatherings usually take place in mid-range hotels, mostly because we can't afford the grand ones, and the small hotels near Zhengjia Muqiao are too embarrassing. Besides, most of our party members are busy making a living in various places. A real "skin talk" conference of our party seems a long way off.

To connect with party members and share information, we often use letters. Therefore, we often address each other as "Skin Brother" or "Skin Fellow," avoiding formal terms like "Esteemed Sir," "Respectfully Yours," "Humbly Announcing," or "Wishing You Well." The content of the letters also strictly adheres to the "Six No's." In this regard, the party's rules are strict, and no one dares to violate them.

When party comrades meet, they always call each other by nicknames, not using terms like "brother." During gatherings, the more jokes told, the better, and the wittier the banter, the better. The goal is to make everyone present laugh until they double over, ensuring that no one is silent or feels lonely.

In short, our party's "skin talk" uses sarcasm, gaining advantages, and speaking "dead talk" (meaningless nonsense) as the only principles. Comrades' parents and mothers-in-law are often the targets of attacks, often causing them distress. In particular, those who seek to gain advantages suffer the most. Therefore, my writing may also have a bit of a flippant tone, and I don't know if I offend others or if I am wrong. This is probably due to the party's training.

When our party comrades are chatting, if a non-member happens to come by and suddenly hears our lively banter, those who are more proper will often blush and be amazed. Those who are slightly unhappy may join in the battle, becoming happy and forgetting their worries. Therefore, I once heard a non-member say that if we could be so happy every day, we would surely live to be eight hundred years old, or at least four or five hundred years old.

Our party member Liao Afeng has a very serious stomach illness. Everyone says he is going to die, and he himself knows he is going to die. But now, not only is he not dead, but he is getting better day by day. Perhaps it is due to the benefits of "skin talk."

If someone is frustrated, in an unpleasant situation, or narrow-minded, joining our party will eliminate all worries and allow them to enter the realm of longevity.

Page 21

Editor's note: Although this article seems like a humorous piece, it is all based on facts. Although they live together all day long, they do not speak of righteousness. However, they do not do evil or wrong either. Therefore, although they gather in groups, they do not rob. Although they are naughty, they do not do evil. Although they are idle, they mostly have jobs. This is why the "Skin Party" is what it is.

Sheep 27

— A Ping

I've been living here for nearly three months, and only yesterday did I discover that behind those two big doors across the street is a large-scale sheep pen. The mystery of the miserable cries I often heard in the middle of the night was also solved.

Yesterday I came home especially late. As I turned into my lane, I was blocked by a flock of sheep, numbering over a hundred. They were all connected by ropes. The leader pulled the end of the rope, dragging them towards the gate, while the people behind waved thin bamboo poles at the sheep. The sheep seemed to know what this gate led to, struggling and trampling on each other, hoping to escape the power of the ropes and bamboo poles. The oppressed cries in the quiet autumn night reminded me of another similar situation.

I had insomnia last night. Usually, when I heard these miserable cries, I hated them for disturbing my good dreams, and I angrily turned over and went back to sleep. But today, having witnessed the scene, the person pulling the rope planted his feet like a boxer, his entire strength extending to his thick arms. He leaned back, forming an acute angle of forty degrees with the ground. The leading sheep, directly affected by the rope, stretched its neck, but its four legs tried hard to retreat. Every sheep was desperately fighting its last battle. In this narrow doorway, the sheep and the people were at odds. However, the bamboo poles rained down on them. Those who were hit tried to retreat, but the second blow came again, and a series of miserable bleats seemed to still be in my ears. Turning and tossing, I couldn't sleep well all night.

When I woke up this morning, I looked at the two doors across the street from the window. Like a stubborn woman, I thought about this problem again. Humans are truly cruel animals. I am naturally a part of this cruelty. Although I have not pulled the rope or waved the bamboo pole, I watched this tragedy with my own eyes, and there was another similar situation. At that time, I just covered my ears. Thinking like this, I seemed to be repenting to this group of sheep! I couldn't help but think of going to the sheep pen to see what was going on. Were the sheep from last night alright?

The old man guarding the gate was very friendly. I told him what I wanted, and he opened the door and led me in. I had just come in from a bright place, and the inside was as dark as hell. Only a foul smell rushed from my nose. After standing firm, I found that there was a skylight of several square feet on the roof, which was the only light in this sheep pen. The sheep pen was very large and divided into many fences. The old man told me that this was the price difference of the sheep. There were more than five hundred sheep in total. Of course, I didn't recognize the sheep from last night, or maybe they had been classified as the owner's investment allocation. There were ten sheep in each fence, and a lot of green grass was laid out in front of them. They were all eating, sleeping, and playing leisurely. The struggle from last night had long since become peaceful.

I regretted it very much when I came back, regretting that I had made a number one fool of myself, suddenly sympathizing with the sheep. Their struggles and miserable cries were because they didn't know there was delicious green grass inside. Moreover, humans use sheep as food, just as a certain type of animal (including humans) uses humans as food. Survival of the fittest is the principle of natural selection. Even if everyone in the world became a fool like me, it would not reverse it. Thinking of my insomnia last night, it was a pointless loss.

A Record of Strolling Through a Department Store 28

— Hong Ben

After submitting a manuscript to the X newspaper, it was still early when I came out. I looked listlessly at the newspaper stand for a while, and then turned to the tram stop at the ball park. I originally wanted to take the tram home. Suddenly, the excitement of the big sale at the X Company across the street shook my heart that wanted to go home. People were squeezed in like sardines, flags were waving in front of the building, and military music was playing urgently. The so-called big sale has never been related to me, but I like to join in the fun. Usually, when I have nothing to do, I am used to strolling around the company. Perhaps this is my philosophy of "better than nothing." Naturally, I should take a trip there.

This is a bit embarrassing. "Running around the company" (suddenly thought) is first running around, flipping through things, and ultimately unable to withstand the employees' disdainful eyes. But I already have considerable experience! ! In addition to flipping through things, I always have to ask about their prices, even though I always "shake my head to end it," it can also show that I have a "want to buy" wish, the wish is so abstract, others can hardly see, only I understand.

When I strolled to the stationery section on the third floor, I bought a small notebook for four cents, so I was also holding a package of goods in my palm. Strolling again, it seemed much more imposing. When walking downstairs, oh, this is really God knows, the spacious cement staircase, people are squeezed like a box of needles, there is simply no room to insert your feet. Seeing that the situation is completely different, the eyes of the public are like hungry eagles, and they are whispering. I have always been indifferent to this situation. The old temper is still there, squeezing to the counter on the second floor, this is when I discovered the secret.

"Look, movie star Chen XX is also here for the big sale!" This seemed to be said by a clerk, the tone was unusually rude, I just explored as much as possible with my eyes, and sure enough, Chen XX was standing in the crowd in front, and even more found that the eyes of the public were all focused on her, the situation was quite tense.

I am very ashamed. I am busy with life all year round, and I only go to the cinema once or twice. However, I also have considerable attention and considerable knowledge of the stars. There are star photos hanging on the wall of my desk, and I also bought a book of phopographs and pasted several star photos that I "yearn for" on weekdays. This is also because of my old temper. I always express my goodwill to girls.

Speaking of Chen XX, although she is not a movie queen, I express considerable goodwill to her. She is an innocent star, and the not-so-big black mole on the corner of her cherry lips often makes me feel "the beauty of imperfection." In the movie, I watched a movie starring her more than half a year ago. Although the character is so innocent and delicate, she is a protagonist who is good at acting in tragic films. You can see it clearly from that movie. I don't know how much sour tears people shed.

As for the real person, she is not necessarily so innocent. She is still as ethereal as she is in the movie, no, even more ethereal than in the movie, in my opinion. This may be influenced by the lover (I assert that it is her lover) and an old woman next to her. Here, she shows a poet's face, with light makeup and light steps, calm and dignified. This is my evaluation after seeing her. Her figure is also fatter than in the movie, no, she is simply a "big head," and the richness and smoothness of her muscles really make people that.

"Oh! She is a movie star after all! She is Chen XX after all!"

I shouted these two sentences in succession, and suddenly everyone squeezed out the door, it turned out that it was already seven o'clock, and the company was about to close. I squeezed out the door, and dusk had shrouded the tempting Nanjing Road. I took the tram home under the neon lights.

People Wandering on the Street 29

— Yi

Tiredness and hunger made Afu unable to sleep for a moment. He stretched his neck, revealing his pair of lifeless eyes, looking at the dark street.

During the day, hundreds and thousands of people walk on this street, but in this late night, it is as quiet as death. There is not a single figure in the darkness. The kerosene lamps in the middle of the road are hung very far away, and their light is dim and faint. The flames are blown up and down by the wind, sometimes bright and sometimes dark, looking like the will-o'-the-wisps on the grave. Darkness and silence occupy the streets late at night.

Afu tiptoed up from under the dark shop porch, rubbed his tired and hungry eyes, and walked step by step on the street. However, hunger made him lose the strength to walk. His legs seemed to weigh a thousand pounds. He barely ran a few dozen steps, and could no longer support it. A burst of darkness in front of him, and he lay down under the shop porch of another store.

He had not eaten for two whole days. At this time, although he felt excessively tired, the hunger in his stomach made him have to squint his eyes, lying on the cement of the shop porch, panting and dazed.

The crowing of chickens in the distance has already reached this silent street, and a little white has appeared in the corner of the sky at the end of the street. Gradually, there are sounds of people walking on the street. The mournful cries of pigs in the butcher shop, and the barking of dogs in the streets and alleys, are heard one after another. Dawn has already arrived in the world.

The shops have opened, and the street has returned to the lively world.

Afu is now also mixed in the crowd, walking slowly, from the front street to the back street, and from the back street to the front street. His pair of yellow hungry eyes, without turning, are all looking at the white rice in the rice shop, the steaming pots in the noodle restaurant, and his stomach is rumbling. Even the steamed buns and sesame cakes in the sesame cake shop, he thinks that being able to eat one is also happiness that is gone.

Finally, he stood at the door of a rice shop on the back street. He watched the people in the shop eating breakfast, and the corners of his mouth kept flowing with foam. The hunger in his stomach made him even more uncomfortable.

He suddenly looked at the pedestrians around him with thief's eyes, tiptoed to the back door of the rice shop, stretched his neck and looked at the window, then pushed open the door and walked in. At this time, his heart was like soybeans baking on the fire, jumping wildly, and his hands and feet were a little unsteady. "God, as long as I can be lucky this time, I will never do it again next time." He secretly blessed like this.

The rice, bag after bag, piled up like a mountain. Although Afu's hands were shaking, hunger oppressed him, so he exhausted all his strength, carried a large bag of rice on his shoulder, and ran out of that terrifying door.

"Catch the thief"

A cry rang out, and Afu's heart was in a panic. Originally, he was already too hungry to have any strength, and a large bag of rice was pressed on his shoulder, so his feet softened and he was caught by two pursuers.

"Catch him, don't let him go. The lost items on the street these days were all stolen by him."

"He really doesn't know how to die. He stole a bag of rice on the front street yesterday, and he's here again today."

People were shouting and scolding in a hubbub, and the idlers walking around also surrounded Afu. A burst of fists hit Afu's body.

The sun hung high in the blue sky, and its light, like nails, shot into Afu's back. He walked one step at a time, thinking:

"Why don't you catch me away? Where can I go to eat, and what about my wife?"

Experimental Education? 30

— Baili

Bastard 31

— Shui Rong

We don't have a mother.

It's really that we don't have a mother. We always suffer losses everywhere, and when we suffer losses, there's nowhere to complain. That feeling is like a mute eating Coptis chinensis (bitter).

For example: the way my younger brother's teachers and classmates treat my younger brother:

Those teachers said behind his back: "Bastard

Page 22

Page 23

!"

Those classmates said in front of him: "Bastard!"

Some embarrassed eyes were shooting at my younger brother, some dirty spit was shooting at my younger brother.

He dragged his book bag horizontally without resistance and ran back: "Brother, they all call me "Bastard!"

Thousands of arrows pierced my heart. Tears appeared in my eyes, and then flowed back in.

I reluctantly replied: "Don't pay attention to them, brother! Remember, one day they will also be bastards."

My younger brother cried and shouted: "Mom! Mom!" Suddenly, he asked: "Why don't I have a mother?"

Well, why don't we have a mother?

Every door is closed in front of us! Everyone's face is turned away in front of us!

Everyone said: "Unlucky, met a bastard!"

Everyone said: "Met a bastard, unlucky!"

Everyone said: "………………!"

Thousands of arrows pierced our hearts, tears appeared in our eyes, and then flowed back in.

Night.

The moon sneaked into my house, looking at me lonely, looking at my lonely shadow on the wall.

Sob, sob, sob—let the tears that I endured during the day flow out!—Sob, sob, sob.

"Why don't we have a mother?"

What answered me was the darkness of silence.

I quietly ran to my mother's room: kissing the bed my mother slept on, kissing the pillow my mother slept on…

"Tell me, why don't we have a mother"

It was the darkness of silence that answered me.

Sob, sob, sob—Sob, sob, sob.

Suddenly, I saw my mother lying on the bed: she was as thin as an Egyptian mummy. Her face was strangely dark and twitching. A thin layer of skin wrapped around her high cheekbones.………Suddenly, she bit her firewood-like arm: "Ah, let me die quickly! I've caused so many special diseases…" Then, she closed her eyes!

"Mom! Mom!" My younger brother's voice.

Mom is gone, it's my younger brother lying on this bed!

"Don't cry, brother! Mom will never come back. Remember: how Mom died. Mom was crushed to death by life! So young! We must never take the path she took again."

"I want Mom!"

I put a pillow next to him and let him lean on it: "Here, brother! Mom here!"

The cover is inscribed by movie queen Chen Yumei, which makes it even more precious. The price remains the same. It is heard that the method of giving fan surfaces to preferential subscribers will be extended to the end of September, and it will still be sold exclusively by the Modern Bookstore.

Novel

Uncle's Braid (2) 32

— Ling He

Uncle Fengyun didn't speak, but only smoked water tobacco. The water tobacco pipe always made a buzzing sound when smoked because it was very dirty, which seemed to take a lot of effort. Shimin climbed down from the high stool at this time. As usual, when guests came, it was his chance to be lazy. In this regard, he had always had a good method: when guests came, he would read aloud with a loud voice, a sharp, piercing sound, which simply made it impossible to hear what people were saying. Then, his father couldn't help but tell him to stop for a while. Then, needless to say, he would quickly lean on his father's side from the desk, listening quietly to the guests' conversation. Sometimes, the guests only talked about things like whether the harvest was good or not, which was very boring. He even took this opportunity to run outside to play. But he didn't use this method today. He simply stopped reading as soon as he saw the guests coming.

Uncle Fengyun smoked several bags of tobacco in a row, and then said slowly:

"Then you read the Shanghai newspapers every day. Is there any news in the newspapers?"

"Are you talking about news about the revolutionaries?" Father said, "Of course, they don't dare to publish it. But there are often things about catching revolutionaries."

"But the world is bound to be in great chaos. A few days ago, I heard about dogs growing horns and chicks growing feet. Yesterday, I looked at the chickens in my house one by one, and two of them had grown feet. Later, I killed them all and ate them."

"Chickens growing feet? Chickens always have feet." Father thought Uncle Fengyun's words were ridiculous. But Fengyun replied:

"Ah, who said chickens don't have feet? What I'm talking about is that two more feet grew in the chickens' wings?"

"Oh! Is there such a thing? That's strange."

As soon as Shimin heard this, he ran to the kitchen in a strange way and shouted loudly:

"Aunt! Come here quickly, come and see if the chickens at home have grown two more feet in their wings?"

Here, Uncle Fengyun also said to the senior teacher:

"If there are any chickens with extra feet, kill them and eat them. It's always troublesome to keep monsters at home."

Soon, the sound of catching chickens was heard. Some were frightened and ran away, and some struggled pitifully in their aunt's hands. After that, the aunt caught two of them and came to the hall from the corridor, asking Uncle Fengyun:

"Where are the feet in the wings? There aren't any, look!"

"Maybe you don't have them at home, but let me take a look." He took the chicken and turned its wings to look for them, "Look, isn't this a foot? This small mole-like thing."

"Ah, is that it?" The aunt said, "Then every chicken has it. If you don't believe me, let's look at this one, it also has it. …Look, right? Isn't there a grain in every wing?"
